< text>
A long-time neighborhood gem, Grandeho's is one of those rare places where the food, personal service and ambiance all stand out... Nothing fancy, but the quality of the food always brings us back.  Featuring a variety of Asian food such as fresh sushi, seafood, noodles, etc.  The owner is a local resident and it's obvious this restaurant is a part of her family, and the hospitality always shines through.  Prices are a little on the high side, but the quality of the food is worth it.< /text>

<user>114711656337281650296<//user>< user_name>
Jennifer Hay< /user_name>
<Date>1472230554411</Date><gmap_id>0x808580e13cd891e9:0x8ef2442c19df560c<//gmap_id></record>

< UserId.>
110826575693431205028< /UserId.>
<Gmap_id>0x808580e13cd891e9:0x8ef2442c19df560c<//Gmap_id>< review>
A true gem in the Wharf district of San Francisco.

My wife and I love to find small local places to dine when we travel, and the hotel concierge suggested this unassuming eatery for "really good sushi".   Grandeho's Kamekyo did not disappoint.  It's not cheap, but the rolls were fresh and service was prompt. Everything we wanted from a casual night out.

There are "hipper" places, and if that's your thing, you might be disappointed.  That's definitely not my thing, though, and it was an easy 2 block walk from our hotel located almost on top of Fisherman's Wharf.

It's worth noting that they do NOT participate in Monterrey Bay Aquarium's "seafood watch" program, so you can get some fish there that are on the "avoid" list.  This is probably no surprise to folks who know about the relationship of the Japanese to Pacific Ocean fishing, but if that's not a problem for you, it was an amazing evening.  If it *is* a problem for you, you can always take the SeaFood Watch app with you and refrain from ordering those items.

Overall, we had a wonderful evening of fresh fish.  I highly recommend a visit if you are in the area and in search of great sushi.<//review>

I don't like they abuse of the customer trust. The final bill includes the tip, which is 18%.
There is a sign at the entrance with low size showing you they will charge the tips. Obviously you will read it (if you have very good vision and you focus to these area) when you finish.
Plates are good but prices are high. And, as I said previously, you will get a big surprise when the ticket comes to your table.
I'm sure I'll never come back here.</text>

Casual mom-and-pop sushi place with friendly service and fresh fish. The wife and I ordered Sushi Boat A ($60), which was the perfect amount of sushi for the both of us. Fresh, good quality fish, and the boat had a great mix of rolls v. sushi v. sashimi. <Rating>4< /Rating><review>Small fitness studio with guided group classes/workouts, boot camp-style. Depending on time of day, you can get from a few people to a crowded room (I believe 24 is the max, which is a lot of people for its small space).

Coaches are friendly and the heart rate monitor workout helps you keep track of your goals and target. I feel that sometimes some of the coaches try to push people to go farther/faster/heavier than they should, but of course you're not forced into it.

Nice premium fitness studio, not for the light of wallet. Similar concept/style in many ways to Barry's Fitness (which is literally across the street from them); except, I like the space at Orangetheory better, because you can see outdoors and it's not a dark, enclosed windowless tunnel like the Barry's across the street.

Overall a really good workout with good facilities and friendly coaches. Really needs more bathrooms/showers (they only have 2 each), but they literally have no more space.< /review>< pics>

< Date>

<Rating>5</Rating>< text>
When my favorite ride Jurassic Park was closing and was being replaced by Jurassic World, I had mix feelings. I loved Jurassic World  and I liked Fallen Kingdom but I didn't want change! 10 months later, I was expecting the ride to be ruined by screens and it would end up like Fast and Furious Supercharged. Fortunately, I was wrong. This is everything I wanted for a Jurassic themed ride. Sure there are screens but they only use it for absolute necessary. It's nice seeing the old anamitronics, as well as seeing new ones too. Especially the indominus Rex. It looks straight out of Jurassic World and steals the show. I have little to no problems with this ride.

Tho, they need to bring back Dilophosaurus for Jurassic World 3. #bringbackthedilophosaurus</text>

< text>
A great ride that I'd recommend to nearly anyone.

Although the wait times are one of the longest within the park, at least Universal tried to keep you entertained with widescreen screens that tell you fun facts, give "interviews" to Jurassic world employees, and more. It was quite a while before I noticed the loop restarted, so plenty of new content to stare at.

The ride itself is pretty neat, and the "big" drop wasn't horrible at all (although the only restraint is one lap bar for the row, so only the person with the biggest legs will be completely secured)

There are lockers to store items in, but at the rather high cost of five dollars, so just wear your bags backwards and hang on to your smaller items. They'll be fine.</text>

Steff A.< /user_name>
<Text>I've been riding Jurassic Park for years but they just leveled up in 2019 and they did good...

The theme is still the same as you're on a boat tour through Jurassic Park  and things go sideways with dinosaurs getting loose.  The dinosaurs movement is much more realistic and less robotic throughout the ride. When your boat starts going vertical to the big drop section, instead of a 'water treatment area' you're heading into 'T-Rex Kingdom'. They added a predator cove in this area as well.
Right before the big drop you come across a FULL Bodied T-Rex fighting it out with another dinosaur.  Before the upgrade, it was just a T-Rex head terrorizing you before you dropped down.  This is much more scary and awesomely realistic.  Well done.

***SPOILER ALERT: I'm about to review the new aquarium section.  If you want to be surprised, stop reading here. =)

At the beginning of the tour, you enter the aquarium observatory.  You come across these massive screens that show case the aquarium and they are awesomely realistic.  You find yourself staring into them as your tour boat peacefully coasts through.  When the massive Mosasaurus appears, it chomps down a shark and aggressively swims around the 'tank'  Then it charges the observation glass at full speed cracking the window and which point water blasts down on the boat.  Choreographed perfectly and it definitely took me by surprise.

It was super popular before the upgrade and even more so.  We waited 20 minutes with the express pass and it was a 3 hour wait via the general admission line.  However you get there, this new Jurassic Tour ride is a definite must see.  Enjoy!< /Text>< pics>
None</pics>

I never thought I would be excited to see the dentist. This place is great! I'm a techie so for me to say I'm impressed by the technology at this office means a lot. < text>
Who would ever think to write a review on a dentist?    Well, due to the fact that every member of my family and my sisters family have all had the privilege of having outstanding dental cleanings, and phenomenal dental work by Dr. Hatch and his staff, I feel compelled to do so.

We have 4 grown kids and not one of them grumble about going to the dentist.  Hmmmmmm..... Could it be that great rock and roll music they play (and Dr. Hatch even sings when he works) or is it the calm talent they all have?

I say a little bit of both...   The family agrees that Scripps Rock Dental.... "ROCKS"!

Dr. Gupta was so helpful with my son when he broke his tooth at a basketball game.....she said come on in, I will work late!   fantastic!

Now me,   ... well years ago I decided that  the numbing shot called Novocaine was overrated, and when I first went to see Dr. Hatch I pleaded with him to allow me to do   my fillings and crowns without the numbing.   He said ..."Ok".  The reality..... It takes a lot of patience to be patient with a patient like me!   He has the skill to calmly do the work, any of you that aren't into the fat face syndrome after the dentist, I would highly recommend  giving it a try!

We will continue to refer anyone that asks.... We did move away from scripps and continue to drive back...they are all just that good!

Oh,   Natalie and Kate and Catherine are fantastic at handling all the insurance details too!  Plus they are always so friendly!

Thanks to all at Scripps Rock!< /text>

On 02/04/2019, I receive a phone call from Heather Peralta stating that I never submitted docs for the bank that I was trying to pull my funds from.  However, I submitted the bank account activity in 12/2018.  Heather admitted in her e-mail that she assumed that I was going to use my Chase account because I had enough funds.  But, the thing is I had more funds in my other account.  So, now, I had to drop everything to close on 02/04/2019.  I was faxing documents to Heather like crazy, even into my lunch break!  Heather didn't even know that I had two accounts from the bank that I was trying to pull my funds.  One account was closed.  She didn't even know that and was asking for statement on the closed account when there was another account that was opened.  I had to tell her that!  She just asked for all the documents even the ones that I already submitted.  When I told her that I already submitted that she responded in her e-mail, "Okay, maybe we don't need that."  She was asking for documents that I submitted in 03/2018 and 09/2018 in 12/2018!  It was terrible working with her!

She e-mailed me saying that she was concluding that I closed on 02/04/2019 because my wire transfer did not come in on time. I believe had Semon done her investigation properly, she should have known that Heather only received the docs on 02/04/2019 which continued into my lunch break. 108481046464471306006< /userid>
<name>John Dyke< /name>< Time>
1532642543870</Time>
< rating>
4< /rating>
< text>
The best answer I can give whenever people ask me what the heck CC&C is I always answer, "It's the poor man's Costco." This is an overly-simplified answer, of course. CC&C is much more than that; it's also a restaurant/party supply store as well. Here's my Top 6 list of favorite things at CC&C:

1) They have the most extensive collection of Torani syrup (they also sell the pumps, too!) that I've ever seen; including quite a few sugar-free varities. If Torani makes it, they have it!

2) Great selection & prices on charcoal briquettes. They have the standard Kingsford, and also carry huge bags of Mesquite charcoal.

3) Their restaurant/kitchen supply area is fantastic. The have everything you could want and then some. From basics like cutting boards and tongs to HUGE stock pots that you could simmer a small hippo in!

4) Nice selection of Mexican and Asian candies and treats. My favorites are the "Yan Yan" and the "Hello Panda" cookies.

5) Nice selection of hot sauces, dried chiles and spices. As someone who likes to add a little "taste" in their cooking, this place is the cure.

6) Great selection of party supplies at terrific prices; they have just about everything you could need to throw a children's party, fiesta or luau.

There's much more than what I've listed above, but you'll just have to go in for yourself and see. Couple all of the above with friendly customer service and you've got a hidden shopping gem in the heart of Ghetto Glen.</text>

< text>
Little ceasar pizza one of the better fast food pizza parlors. I prefer it over domino's or pizza hut because the dough tastes better. I am also old school all I want is cheese and theirs is not greasy. Also their square pie (deep dish) reminds me of Sicilian style from back on the east coast. This site does have the pizza portal so your pie stay hot till you pick it up. I only gave 3 stars because of location especially at night it is not the best place to be. Otherwise I would give it  5 stars for the food is good, fast service and the staff friendly.</text>
